    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bb169efe-37b3-42af-b24d-6a1892442edd'
      });

  <span id="freeText7916014045363087354" style="display:none"><strong>In the instant <em>New York Times</em> bestseller that started the Dark Elements series, one kiss is enough to kill…</strong><br /><br />Layla just wants to fit in at school and go on a date with Zayne, whom she's crushed on since forever. Trouble is, Zayne treats Layla like a sister—and Layla is a half demon, half gargoyle with abilities no one else possesses. And even though Zayne is a Warden, part of the race of gargoyles tasked with keeping humanity safe, Layla's kiss will kill anything with a soul—including him.<br /><br />Then she meets Roth—a demon who claims to know her secrets. Though Layla knows she should stay away, it's tough when that whole no-kissing thing isn't an issue. Trusting Roth could ruin her chances with Zayne, but as Layla discovers she's the reason for a violent demon uprising, kissing the enemy suddenly pales in comparison to the looming end of the world.<br /><br /><strong>"Armentrout works her magic with swoon-worthy guys and a twist you never see coming."—#1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling author Abbi Glines</strong><br /><br /><strong>"Armentrout is a major talent... <div id="review_822067797" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/822067797" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/822067797?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17455585-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=religious-spiritual">religious-spiritual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer822067797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9027669567935246382"><blockquote>
  <i>"Not everyone is created equal.”<br/>I pursed my lips. “I don’t think I’m special.”<br/>Roth looked at me again. “But you are. You’re a half demon that is also half Warden."</i>
</blockquote>This is standard Armentrout. <b>Fans of her books will love it, people who wants something a little less...formulaic, like me, will be disappointed.</b> I keep reading her books, hoping that something will change for the better. So far, nothing had.<br/><br/>This book is about gargoyles and demons. But don't get the wrong impression. It's less this</span>
  <span id="freeText9027669567935246382" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Not everyone is created equal.”<br>I pursed my lips. “I don’t think I’m special.”<br>Roth looked at me again. “But you are. You’re a half demon that is also half Warden."</i>
</blockquote>This is standard Armentrout. <b>Fans of her books will love it, people who wants something a little less...formulaic, like me, will be disappointed.</b> I keep reading her books, hoping that something will change for the better. So far, nothing had.<br><br>This book is about gargoyles and demons. But don't get the wrong impression. It's less this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393483358ra/8720269.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And more this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393483358ra/8720270.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is standard Armentrout in that:<br><br>1. The main heroine is the <b>star of the show</b>, there is no doubt about it, the universe revolves around her and only her<br><br>2. There is <b>slut-shaming</b>. There is an ample <b>shortage of meaningful female friendship</b>, there is plenty of <b>slutty girls</b> around, including her best friend, all designed to <b>make the heroine seem virginal, chaste, and pure in contrast</b><br><br>3. The heroine is <b>special, different</b>, one of a kind, due to <b>only the fact that she was born to an extraordinary heritage; she does nothing to earn our respect</b><br><br>4. There is a <b>love triangle</b>, and further than that, almost every eligible person with a penis around her age range <b>wants her milkshake</b><br><br>5. There is <b>more flirting than plot</b><br><br>6. The heroine is <b>supposed to be kick-ass, but she is rescued all the fucking time</b><br><br>The good:<br><br>1. The writing is enjoyable, the book itself is a light, quick read<br><br>2. The setting is a predictable, light, traditional Urban Fantasy with characters we don't see too often---gargoyes (but the book still needs more garrgoyles and less hot-men-outside-of-stone-form)<br><br><u>The Summary</u>: Gargoyles exist. They are called Wardens. 10 years ago, they came out in public. <b>The world knows that gargoyles exist now, and there's surprisingly little hullabaloo about it.</b> Miley Cyrus twerkin' on Robin Thicke's crotch got a more shocked reaction than we were shown in this book.<blockquote>
  <i>...the Wardens went public ten years ago. The Alphas had ordered the Wardens to come out of the shadows. To humans, Wardens had come out of their stone shells. After all, the gargoyles adorning many churches and buildings had been carved to resemble a Warden in his true skin.</i>
</blockquote>Huh, gargoyles exist. Ok.<br><br>Layla is 17 years old. She is beautiful, but doesn't really consider herself that pretty. I mean, Layla only looks like an elf-princess. What's so special about that?<blockquote>
  <i>Zayne said I looked like the long-lost sister of the elf in Lord of the Rings. That was a huge confidence booster. Sigh.</i>
</blockquote>Sigh, indeed. <b>Fuck, it must be so horrible to go through life all blonde and elfin, looking like Legolas' sister.</b> Tough existence, man. To top it off, she's in love with a gorgeous Warden guy (Zayne) who only sees her as a sister. A really hot sister with whom he loves going on coffee dates.<br><br>Layla is special. She is half-Demon, half-Warden. She looks like a human and she cannot shift into a monster-like stone gargoyle form because she is a half-blood. <b>Therefore, Layla is half-blood, all beautiful. Special without the ugly side effects of being a gargoyle-like Guardian.</b><br><br>Layla is an orphan (oh hello there, trope). She has amnesia (trope). She doesn't know anything about her birth or her parents (trope). Her Warden guardians keep everything a secret from her (trope). One day, while stupidly chasing down a minor demon into a dark alley, Layla nearly gets killed. She is rescued by a dark, handsome, sexy Upper Level Demon. <b>His name is Roth. He has a snake named Bambi.</b> I don't mean to say his penis is named Bambi, I mean he has a snake tattoo that comes to life whose name is Bambi.<blockquote>
  <i>No—not a mass, but a huge freaking snake at least ten feet long and as wide as I was.<br>The thing spun toward me, rising halfway up. Its eyes burned an unholy red.<br>“Don’t be scared of Bambi,” the demon said. “She’s only curious and maybe a little bit hungry.”<br>The thing was named Bambi?</i>
</blockquote>Sexy Demon Roth starts showing up everyfuckingwhere Layla goes. She goes to school. He's there. He shows up whenever she needs help, like a demonic guardian angel.<br><br>Where I'm from, we call that <b>a fucking stalker</b>. Layla knows that. She trusts him anyway.<blockquote>
  <i>“You don’t? I was following you.”<br>“Oh, so you’re a demon and a stalker?” I swallowed hard. “Because that’s not creepy or anything.”</i>
</blockquote>Oh, he's not just a stalker, he's a pervert, too.<blockquote>
  <i>He leaned in again, his lips brushing the curve of my cheek. “Let me suggest more appropriate places. I have this piercing—”</i>
</blockquote>Oh, wait, there's a reason he's following her. <b>Layla is special.</b> She was born to a special destiny, and he was meant to protect her.<blockquote>
  <i>Roth let out a low breath. “Your mother was known by many names...And because of that, you’re on Hell’s Most Wanted List.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Naturally, Layla is inclined to believe the stranger she just met over the people who have raised her for the past 10 years.</b> Roth and Layla kiss, they flirt, they go out on dates. They spend nights together, staring longingly into each other's eyes. They go to bed together---but they just talk, because demons are such gentlemen that way.<br><br>What is <i>The Lesser Key of Solomon?</i> More importantly, will the two hot, gorgeous men in her life ever stop fighting over Layla?<blockquote>
  <i>Zayne’s grip relaxed. “Shut up.”<br>Roth came to his feet fluidly. “I don’t think I like your tone.”<br>“And I don’t like your face,” Zayne returned.<br>The amount of testosterone the two were throwing off was ridiculous.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Girl-Hate</u>: <b>There's room for only one good girl in this book, and that girl is Layla.</b> Layla is virginal, pure. Layla and her best friend Stacey tease each other by calling each other names. Stacey is, of course, presented as the slut, the <b>hobag</b>, while innocent Layla is the <b>virgin</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>Stacey only blinked, looking like she was coming out of some kind of bizarre trance. I scribbled <b>hobag</b> across her notes. She laughed and wrote <b>virgin ice princess</b> across mine.</i>
</blockquote>Even an insult, a tease, is designed to make Layla look good against her slutty best friend Stacey.<br><br><b>Stacey is sex on wheels.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Stacey started to tug her shirt up as a shield, but must’ve realized there wasn’t enough material there.</i>
</blockquote>She dresses sexily, and the book presents it to us as a bad thing.<blockquote>
  <i>Stacey was saying as she threw herself into her seat. “I didn’t sneak out of the house dressed like this for no good reason.”<br>“No doubt.” I eyed her short skirt and then her cleavage. “We wouldn’t want your boobs to go to waste.”</i>
</blockquote>Stacey constantly makes sexual jokes and gestures.<blockquote>
  <i>“Great!” Stacey chirped, backing off and gesturing wildly behind Roth. She was doing something with her hand and mouth that I knew Roth would be oh so down for.</i>
</blockquote>She is presented as a good friend, but so completely hypersexualized compared to Layla. Her character is insiduously presented as not as good, due to her sexualization.<br><br>The other female characters in the book are either stupid sluts (Eva, the glammed up hobag Mean Girl classmate) or a scared female Warden (never mind that she's also a badass warrior herself), or a nice, beautiful Warden girl who's meant to be hated because of her interest in Layla's first love, Zayne. Danika is nice, but everything she does is seem as mean, an attack on Layla when all she wants to do is be helpful.<blockquote>
  <i>I dumped the stuff in the garbage can, shoulders stiff. “I’m not going to jump on you and suck out your soul, if that’s what you’re worried about.”<br>Danika gasped. “That’s not what I meant—not at all. It’s just that you look like you need something and I want to help.”</i>
</blockquote>Everytime a female character outside of Layla does something remotely normal and nice, Layla snaps at her. There is no room in this book for a positive female figure besides Layla.<br><br><u>The Setting</u>: It's your traditional Urban Fantasy, with Angels, Demons, all that good stuff. This book breaks no molds in the setting. It is completely predictable in this sense, and that's just fine. We have Fiends, we have Posers (demons, heh), we have Zombies. Nothing out of the ordinary.<br><br><b>What I do not like</b>: The setting in this book is anticlimactic. There are gargoyles, humans know they exist...and there's an odd sense of "so what?" about it. People aren't exactly freaking out. There's a church rallying against Wardens...<blockquote>
  <i>Every so often the Church of God’s Children held a rally against the Wardens and then made headlines. They’d been doing it ever since the public had found out about the Wardens’ existence.</i>
</blockquote>And that's the last we hear about it. <b>The book is so centered around Layla and Layla only, so much that the outside world becomes completely secondary and almost gathers no mention in the book.</b><br><br>The setting itself has gaps. There are Wardens...gargoyles...but <b>almost no instance of actual gargoyles in the book. We rarely see the Wardens in action.</b> It's more internal politics and living with the Wardens in human form than anything else.<br><br>There's also the unbelievable case of "OH HUMANS KNOW ABOUT WARDENS BUT LET'S HIDE THE FACT THAT DEMONS EXIST!" <br><br><b>Wut?</b><blockquote>
  <i>The world would descend into chaos if humans knew demons were ordering their morning coffee right alongside them.</i>
</blockquote>Ok, so you're telling me that the world is ok with the existence of gargoyles, that stone men can come to life, but they'd completely freak out if they knew about the existence of demons?<br><br><b>Wut?</b><br><br><u>Layla, you've got me on my knees</u>: *lyric from Eric Clapton*<br><br>Everyone with a dick loves Layla. From hot, protective brother-figure Zayne. Zayne, who always wants to reassure Layla that she is good, despite what Layla thinks of herself.<blockquote>
  <i>Zayne’s eyes flicked up. They seemed brighter than usual. “You’re...perfect just the way you are.”</i>
</blockquote>To schoolboy Gareth.<blockquote>
  <i>“Wow, he is so checking you out.”<br>“Huh?” I looked at Stacey. “Who?”<br>She glanced over her shoulder as she pulled me closer. “The guy you almost plowed into—Gareth Richmond. He’s still checking you out."</i>
</blockquote>To evil pervert Petr who wants her body.<blockquote>
  <i>The line of his jaw hardened. “I didn’t do anything wrong.”<br>“You didn’t do anything wrong? I told you to stop and you wouldn’t—”<br>“You were being a tease.” His voice dropped low. “And since when do demons really get a say in anything?”</i>
</blockquote>To Roth. Roth, who only has eyes for Layla.<br><br>Oh, <b>the love triangle</b>...<blockquote>
  <i>“I...” I didn’t know. I loved Zayne, but I didn’t know what kind of love that was, and Roth... I thought I could be in love with him, if given time. Or maybe I already was, in a little way. “I don’t know.”</i>
</blockquote>It's enjoyable, but only as brain candy. If you're looking for more plot, more substance, I wouldn't recommend this. The character development and plausibility of the plot is absolutely lacking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9027669567935246382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_847563816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847563816" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/847563816?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17455585-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847563816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13025522128625020973"><b>I. Could. Not. Finish. This.</b><br/>I tried. And then I tried some more. But nope, not happening.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394605991i/8876404.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You know what? Perfection really is boring. Perfection is meaningless, unrealistic and <u>so fucking boring</u>. <br/><br/>Armentrout tries to create perfection. A perfectly all-good, virginal, amazing, everyone-wants-to-bone-me, kickass heroine who faultlessly exists at the centre of the universe, while beautiful, perfectly-sculpted, hot boys just orbit around her constantly. It's boring. And you know what else perfection i</span>
  <span id="freeText13025522128625020973" style="display:none"><b>I. Could. Not. Finish. This.</b><br>I tried. And then I tried some more. But nope, not happening.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394605991i/8876404.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what? Perfection really is boring. Perfection is meaningless, unrealistic and <u>so fucking boring</u>. <br><br>Armentrout tries to create perfection. A perfectly all-good, virginal, amazing, everyone-wants-to-bone-me, kickass heroine who faultlessly exists at the centre of the universe, while beautiful, perfectly-sculpted, hot boys just orbit around her constantly. It's boring. And you know what else perfection is? <b>It's all tell and no fucking show.</b><br><br>So this girl - Layla - is amazing, right? She's so SPESHUL. Gifted. Wonderful. Beautiful. We are told all of this and yet never shown examples of it. She's special because she was born into it, not because she does any damn thing to prove it. She's amazing, we are told, but I'm still uncertain what's really so special about her in action. Everyone wants this girl, we are told, but god only knows why. Oh, and she's totally badass... apparently. Maybe I would have noticed if she wasn't so busy being saved all the time.<br><br>Then there's that <b>love triangle</b> *yawn*. I think the descriptions of men are often what separate the romance stories I actually enjoy from the ones that bore me to tears. To be honest, there's a part of me that thinks "yeah, okay, whatever" with this whole male perfection malarkey. These men/boys are beautiful in every way. They are fucking perfect. Their bodies are sculpted awesomeness of muscle and unblemished skin. Their hair falls perfectly in gorgeous thick waves. Their faces were built by angels and they always have a sexy phrase handy to raise the heat levels in any given scene. But I suppose it's hard to criticise this trend when you compare it to the airbrushed, photoshopped and hairless beauties shown in men's magazines. Why shouldn't women get their fantasy perfection? No reason I can see.<br><br><u>Except... it's fucking boring</u>. These men are too perfect for me to care about and fall in love with. I cannot believe in that level of perfection. They are male Barbie dolls, straight off the factory production line. <b>Polished, flawless, perfection</b>. I'd find it easier to love them if they were ugly. I'd also find it easier to love them if Layla took a break from describing their physical perfection for a second and gave them a personality that goes beyond trying to get in her pants (like every male in this book). So many times I felt like me and Layla were having this exchange...<br><br><b>Me:</b> Plot?<br><b>Layla:</b> Fuck the plot. Let's make out!<br><br>There's also a whole bunch of slut-shaming, which I assume is only supposed to emphasise the heroine's purity and goodness. Even her best friend seems like a tool constantly being used to reinforce the MC's good girl persona - her characterisation consists almost solely of her overt sexuality and revealing outfit choices. If the female character is not Layla or a "slut", then she's the evil bitch who has a thing for one of the guys. <br><br>Then I come to some of the ridiculous dialogue between the characters. Look, I know teenagers can be annoying. Insufferable, some might say. Sometimes I read the diaries I wrote from when I was 15 and, oh my god, the angst! It burns! They're hilarious and melodramatic, of course. But still, high school wasn't that long ago for me. And the dialogue between the teens in this book is like what middle-aged adults *think* teenagers might say.<br><br><b>
  <i>Stacey groaned. “I can’t believe Mr. Leto wouldn’t let us do our classics report on Twilight. It is a classic.”</i>
</b><br><br>No one says that. No one. Plus, <i>Twilight</i> isn't even "cool" among high school teens. <i>Twilight</i>, if it is talked about, is the thing girls whisper and giggle about behind their hands. Kids do not announce loudly and openly that <i>Twilight</i> is a classic. <br><br>And don't even get me started on all the male posturing going on, it was laughable. My favourite was this bit:<br><br><i>
  <b>Zayne’s grip relaxed. “Shut up.”<br>Roth came to his feet fluidly. “I don’t think I like your tone.”<br>“And I don’t like your face,” Zayne returned.<br>The amount of testosterone the two were throwing off was ridiculous.</b>
</i><br><br>The thing I find so funny is that this is considered some big, testosterone-fuelled alpha male battle. It sounds more like the fights me and my sister have over music in the car. Maybe you should read this book if you want a good laugh.<br><br>I'm sorry, guys. I know a lot of people love Armentrout and this could be a light, entertaining read for you if you like all her usual elements. But I find it all too formulaic, recycled and... boring. I wish the hype for her books was easier to resist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13025522128625020973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1107439147" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107439147" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107439147?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17455585-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=unoriginal">unoriginal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107439147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11342063835847385827">You know what I've figured out? Jennifer L. Armentrout is a panderer. Meaning, she always writes the same formulaic stuff and always has to have extremely hot, six-foot-something bad boys that are there to solely make the main character's--and the young teen female reader's--panties melt.<br/><br/>What do I have to say to that? Well, first of all,<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416282944ra/11928475.gif' height='200' width='370' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Secondly, here are a few examples of her not-even-a-little-bit-subtle pattern:<br/><br/><b>Taken from the blurb of <i>Wait for You</i>:</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Cameron Hamilton is <b>six feet and three inc</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11342063835847385827" style="display:none">You know what I've figured out? Jennifer L. Armentrout is a panderer. Meaning, she always writes the same formulaic stuff and always has to have extremely hot, six-foot-something bad boys that are there to solely make the main character's--and the young teen female reader's--panties melt.<br><br>What do I have to say to that? Well, first of all,<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416282944ra/11928475.gif" height="200" width="370" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Secondly, here are a few examples of her not-even-a-little-bit-subtle pattern:<br><br><b>Taken from the blurb of <i>Wait for You</i>:</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Cameron Hamilton is <b>six feet and three inches</b> of <b>swoon-worthy</b> hotness, complete with a pair of <b>striking blue eyes</b> and a <b>remarkable ability to make her want things</b> she believed were irrevocably stolen from her. She knows she needs to stay away from him, but Cam is freaking everywhere, with his charm, his witty banter, and that damn dimple that’s just so… so lickable. Getting involved with him is <b>dangerous</b>, but when ignoring the <b>simmering tension</b> that sparks whenever they are around each other <b>becomes impossible</b>, he brings out a side of her she never knew existed."</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Taken from the blurb of her new book <i>Wicked</i>:</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Ren Owens is the last person Ivy expected to enter her rigidly controlled life. He’s <b>six feet and three inches</b> of temptation and <b>swoon-inducing</b> charm. With <b>forest-green eyes</b> and a smile that’s surely left a stream of broken hearts in its wake, he has an <b>uncanny, almost unnatural ability to make her yearn</b> for everything he has to offer. But letting him in is as <b>dangerous</b> as hunting the cold-blooded killers stalking the streets. Losing the boy she loved once before had nearly destroyed her, but the <b>sparking tension</b> that grows between them <b>becomes impossible</b> for Ivy to deny. Deep down, she wants… she needs more than what her duty demands of her, what her past has shaped for her."</i>
</blockquote><br>And I don't think I need to discuss the blurb of this one. There's fucking <i>two</i> hot--and I quote once more, <b>"swoon-worthy"</b>--guys. A love triangle, a.k.a. the YA trope that practically screams "cash grab".<br><br>Okay, I get that all of this pays the bills and all, and that's fine. Everyone's gotta eat. Do whatcha gotta do and all that jazz. But I'm definitely no longer a fan of hers now that I've got a feel of what she's all about. I'd rather support authors who are willing to take risks and think outside of the box (e.g. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6559113.Eliza_Crewe" rel="nofollow noopener">Eliza Crewe</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7105371.Leah_Raeder" rel="nofollow noopener">Leah Raeder</a>, upon recent memory) rather than strictly follow a formula for the sole purpose of filling their pockets. I'm sure she's a lovely person, but as an author she brings nothing new to the table. In fact, she does the exact opposite of that. She pulls out all the old tricks and tries to fluff 'em up as best as possible. To me that's just not cute. It makes her seem like, as an author, she's all about the money money money.<br><br>What makes me sad is that it's not just Jen here who does this. Not even close. This has been a trend in YA for years, and thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4622890-emily-may" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily May's</a> <i>NA Experiment</i>, I pretty much stay away from new adult books in general due to the fact that nearly <i>every</i> NA book follows this formula. They're there to pander, and "originality" is not in their vocabulary. What crushes me is that this kinda shit <i>sells</i>. They sell like hot cakes, and because of this, it's rubbing off even more on YA as well--case in point, this book right here.<br><br>Again, before you fans rip me apart, I have <i>nothing</i> against her as a person. She seems like a nice lady. I'm strictly viewing her as an author and the clear pattern that her work shows. I have to call a spade a spade.<br><br>Sorry 'bout it.<br><br><b>P.S.</b> Shout out to all the authors out there who do your thing and don't conform. You have no idea how valuable you guys are. To me, and to tons of other readers. Keep on keepin' on, and YOU BETTA WERK! &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="11342063835847385827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783399313?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783399313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5188562341901256272">if you know me, you know i love JLAs stories with nearly every fibre of my being but i was hesitant to pick this up, only because it just didnt really interest me. the only reason i did is because <i>‘storm and fury’</i> (a spin off) comes out soon, and it actually sounds really good. so here i am. <br/><br/>fortunately, this turned out better than i thought it would. as someone who is still slowly, but somewhat successfully, immersing themselves into the paranormal genre, gargoyles just seemed a bit much. but i</span>
  <span id="freeText5188562341901256272" style="display:none">if you know me, you know i love JLAs stories with nearly every fibre of my being but i was hesitant to pick this up, only because it just didnt really interest me. the only reason i did is because <i>‘storm and fury’</i> (a spin off) comes out soon, and it actually sounds really good. so here i am. <br /><br />fortunately, this turned out better than i thought it would. as someone who is still slowly, but somewhat successfully, immersing themselves into the paranormal genre, gargoyles just seemed a bit much. but it actually isnt that cheesey. i just think that JLA has the power to write about anything and i will really enjoy it. <br /><br />however, some points are marked off for the love triangle (or strong hint, thereof). im not really a fan and dont understand their purpose. usually i can tolerate them for the sake of reading because i favour one guy over the other, but it annoys me to no end when i end up liking both of the guys. all it does is make me resent the girl for stringing them both along, and thats exactly what i think is gonna happen with this story. <br /><br />but still, this was entertaining and my interest is now piqued as to how the story is going to play out.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373211104" href="/book/show/18006096-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=1-2-stars-read">1-2-stars-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631597809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16795929632238873342">My Roth, Layla and Zayne:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395407317i/8991496._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Layla is half-demon, half-Warden. But brought up by Wardens, daily fighting her demon urges, she hates everything demon-connected. But what happens when her perception of demons is ruined forever?</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395407317i/8991497._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I am not sure what happened here. I love JLA and all her previous paranormal stories. But this one did not live up to my expectations.</b> <br/><br/>So what was my biggest problem with this book? It wasn't the love triangle or the fact that heroine was perfect example of damsel in distress. N</span>
  <span id="freeText16795929632238873342" style="display:none">My Roth, Layla and Zayne:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395407317i/8991496._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Layla is half-demon, half-Warden. But brought up by Wardens, daily fighting her demon urges, she hates everything demon-connected. But what happens when her perception of demons is ruined forever?</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395407317i/8991497._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I am not sure what happened here. I love JLA and all her previous paranormal stories. But this one did not live up to my expectations.</b> <br><br>So what was my biggest problem with this book? It wasn't the love triangle or the fact that heroine was perfect example of damsel in distress. No. It was the fact that most of the banters and dialogues between characters were super-cheesy and childlish. There were so many clichés it wasn't even funny. And action was almost non-existent or really boring. It took 80% (and whole week of reading) until I was at least a bit hooked in the story. And that was just too late for me.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395407317i/8991498._SY540_.jpg" width="310" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>When it comes to "love triangle" in this book, there was only one guy for me. And after reading this book, I am <b>Team Roth</b> all the way. Zayne who? Roth was definitely the best part of this book. A big contradiction. Cocky and arrogant, yet caring and self-sacrificing. I really enjoyed those parts of the book when he was present.<br><br>However, question remains. Who will win Layla's heart at the end? I am definitely curious to see how will this series develop and what direction will JLA take it. Last couple of chapters proved, that she knows how to capture my attention with her writing. She will have her chance with book #2 to either win me over or lost me forever when it comes to The Dark Elements.<br><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>
</a><br><br>*********************************************************<br><br><b>Seems like this woman writes one book per month. But I am not complaining, I love every single story she wrote so far and I cannot wait for this one! :)</b></span>

<div id="review_724973327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724973327" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1045077547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1045077547" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1045077547?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373211104" href="/book/show/18006096-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=strong-female-characters">strong-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=hot-male-characters">hot-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=i-laughed-hard">i-laughed-hard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=cute-book-couple">cute-book-couple</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1045077547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10692691484380002284"> <i>
  <b>"You need something," he said, and when I stared at him, he added, "Your face."<br/><br/>"My face?"<br/><br/>"It's in need of my kisses."</b>
</i> <br/><br/>Who would've thought that demons are kind of hot? *sigh* <br/><br/>If there's one thing that makes this book beautiful and interesting. It's Roth. Roth. And ROTH.<br/><br/>White Hot Kiss is all kinds of awesomesauce. I love the concept Ms. Jennifer L. Armentrout put life into this book. The existence of demons and Wardens (Gargoyles who protect mankind from demons) is a thing that very much cat</span>
  <span id="freeText10692691484380002284" style="display:none"> <i>
  <b>"You need something," he said, and when I stared at him, he added, "Your face."<br /><br />"My face?"<br /><br />"It's in need of my kisses."</b>
</i> <br /><br />Who would've thought that demons are kind of hot? *sigh* <br /><br />If there's one thing that makes this book beautiful and interesting. It's Roth. Roth. And ROTH.<br /><br />White Hot Kiss is all kinds of awesomesauce. I love the concept Ms. Jennifer L. Armentrout put life into this book. The existence of demons and Wardens (Gargoyles who protect mankind from demons) is a thing that very much catches attention. Not necessarily original, but somehow, it's spectacular.<br /><br />While reading this book I felt like I'm in a roller coaster ride. There were lots of actions. And I mean, live, real, intense actions! <br /><br />JLA also did not fail to introduce me to her super swoony characters. And speaking of swoony characters, I'm talking about Roth and no other. Zayne? Nah. Never mind. I kind of don't like him. I don't know why JLA tried to make him the third party of a love triangle but seriously, I don't like it. I just want Roth and Layla. End of the story.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"I lost myself the moment I found you.</b>
</i><br /><br />White Hot Kiss is cheesy and darkly romantic. Roth and Layla's interactions are epically sweet and fantastic. I love their first encounter! It's something I simply can't forget. :) Apart from the romantic side, this book also has funny moments and I found myself really laughing at some point. Talk about the JLA humor... :D <br /><br />Anyways, I love this book. I just wished it wasn't that slow-paced at first, 'coz I admit it didn't get me instantly. I had to patiently read until the final chapters of the book to get my full attention. Because honestly, the best parts were at the final chapters. But all in all, it was a great and fun read. And I need to read the second book soon!<br /><br />Rating: 4 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10692691484380002284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635155262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3445212081675021854"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420433._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='40' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Title:</b> White Hot Kiss<br/><b>Series:</b> Dark Elements #1<br/><b>Author:</b> Jennifer L Armentrout<br/><b>Release Date: </b> February 24, 2014<br/><b>Rating:</b> 4 stars<br/><b>Cliffhanger:</b>. Yes<br/><b> HEA: </b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Not yet  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420434._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='40' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>White Hot Kiss is another YA paranormal romance by Jennifer L Armentrout and as every previous book by this author, this novel doesn’t let go even for a single minute. It’s one of those keeping you on the edge till the last page stories that will make you laugh, feel sad and angry as well as introduce you to amazi</span>
  <span id="freeText3445212081675021854" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420433._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Title:</b> White Hot Kiss<br><b>Series:</b> Dark Elements #1<br><b>Author:</b> Jennifer L Armentrout<br><b>Release Date: </b> February 24, 2014<br><b>Rating:</b> 4 stars<br><b>Cliffhanger:</b>. Yes<br><b> HEA: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Not yet  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391618077i/8420434._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>White Hot Kiss is another YA paranormal romance by Jennifer L Armentrout and as every previous book by this author, this novel doesn’t let go even for a single minute. It’s one of those keeping you on the edge till the last page stories that will make you laugh, feel sad and angry as well as introduce you to amazing set of surprises, unexpected twists and turns and yes it does have a pretty perfect boy… or even two boys to swoon over. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393612433i/8740104.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Layla is half demon and half Warden a creature similar to gargoyle. From the time she was seven she was raised by Wardens that for most part hate her and her demon’s side. Why? Because demons are their natural enemies. The only Warden who cares about her is Zayne, Layla’s secret crush.<br> <br>What’s more Layla is dangerous; she craves human and wardens’ souls. One kiss or being close enough to kiss and she won’t be able to stop herself from sucking of someone’s soul. <br><br>When she reaches seventeen years old something weird start to happen to her. The demons are after her and there is mysterious Upper Level Demon that just saved her life and goes to her school…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393612433i/8740105.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was definitely not what I expected or hoped for. Armentrout went into completely different direction which was as much surprising as exciting. I can’t say I was bored or didn’t like how easily yet thrilling the story seemed to flow. Even when I thought things started to calm down I was quickly thrown into another bumpy ride. <br><br>The characters as always were witty, funny and adorable. I loved all of them. Layla was strong and feisty but in completely different way than Alex from Covenant Series of Kathy from Lux Series. She was less impulsive or reckless, yet still she was kickass heroine with impressive backbone and pure heart. <br><br><i>
  <b>Roth stared at me, looking sort of stunned. “I didn’t know you had it in you.”<br>“What?”<br>He tapped the tip of my nose. “You’re feisty underneath all that fluff.”<br>“I’m not sure if I should be offended or not,”</b>
</i><br><br>The way she was treated by Wardens and humans made me feel bad for her. She was very lonely and unwanted. The only person that seemed to like and care for her was Zayne. After she met Roth things seemed to pick up for her and I was so glad she finally could be truly herself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393612640i/8740133.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was a afraid of how the love triangle will look here – usually I hate them and reading about them makes me nauseous. Here, I didn’t mind it much. In my eyes, Layla already made her choice and I hope it’ll stay the same. <br><br>Zayne was a good friend. Loyal, sweet and caring. I liked him, but he was not the one that made me all hot and bothered.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393612433i/8740108.jpg" width="400" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>It was the sexy demon called Roth that made me go all gaga. He was a little bit cocky, arrogant and bad in the best possible way. His comments made me laugh or smile. He was just perfect! *sigh*<br><br><i>
  <b>“See, I was raised in Hell. You could say I’m socially awkward.”</b>
</i><br><br>Overall, it’s very good young adult book. Sexy in JLA’s way, funny, exciting and action packed!<br>Why not five then? I just craved a little bit more romance than there was, I hope the next books will deliver it!<br><br><br><b>FOLLOW SMOKIN HOT BOOK BLOG ON: <b><br><br><a href="https://twitter.com/BlogSmokin/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Twitter" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391768351i/8452934.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="Google Plus" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391768485i/8452964.png"     <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032748327?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/9871824-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9871824-ash?shelf=owned-e-reader">owned-e-reader</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032748327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11988158531324211394"><i>first read: March 16-17, 2015.<br/>first reread: July 25-27, 2015<br/>second reread: March 20-22, 2016</i><br/><br/><b>JULY 2015:</b> These books are just so fun. I loved it still, maybe not AS much as I did the first time I read this 4 months ago, BUT it wasn't enough to affect the 5 star rating. <br/><blockquote>
  <i>“The newcomer stood well over six feet, as tall as any Warden. His hair was dark, the color of obsidian, and it reflected blue in the dim light. Lazy locks slipped over his forehead and curled just below his ears. Brows arched ov</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11988158531324211394" style="display:none"><i>first read: March 16-17, 2015.<br />first reread: July 25-27, 2015<br />second reread: March 20-22, 2016</i><br /><br /><b>JULY 2015:</b> These books are just so fun. I loved it still, maybe not AS much as I did the first time I read this 4 months ago, BUT it wasn't enough to affect the 5 star rating. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The newcomer stood well over six feet, as tall as any Warden. His hair was dark, the color of obsidian, and it reflected blue in the dim light. Lazy locks slipped over his forehead and curled just below his ears. Brows arched over golden eyes and his cheekbones were broad and high. He was attractive. Very attractive. Mind-bendingly beautiful, actually, but the sardonic twist to his full lips chilled his beauty. The black T-shirt stretched across his chest and flat stomach. A huge tattoo of a snake curled around his forearm, the tail disappearing under his sleeve and the diamond-shaped head rested on the top of his hand. He looked my age. Total crush material—if it wasn’t for the fact that he had no soul.” </i>
</blockquote><br />Roth and Layla are just so entertaining. Their scenes together are definitely my favorites. I've noticed that JLA likes to use the same weird exclamation remarks in all her books...those, I actually found rather annoying...but other than that, I heart Roth lots and lots and lots, he's definitely still top 5 book boyfriend material. Zayne didn't really bug me the first time I read this, but after having read the 2nd one and deciding I was definitely <b>not</b> 'Team Zayne'....I decided I didn't really like his parts in this book the 2nd time around. <br /><br />The cliffhanger here, even though it isn't so much of a cliffhanger because I already know what happens...it still killed me...I am pretty sure I felt my heart break a little bit. I love books that can bring out such emotions, even on, <i>especially</i> on a reread.<br /><br />I am really, really, really excited for the release of Every Last Breath!!!! It comes out in about 24 hours and I am beyond fucking ready to figure out what happens!! <br /><br />----------<br /><br /><b>MARCH 16 &amp; 17, 2015:</b> <s> I just....<b>absolutely heart JLA</b>! She is probably one of my <i>favorite</i> authors. This book was awesome, haha, I <u>loved, SO TOTALLY LOVED</u>, the sarcastic, witty, arrogant, cocky main characters..... Damn cliffhanger, <b>I am like...crying my eyes out over here....It was happy happy happy, and hilarious....until it was heartbreaking....</b> on to the next one!!!!!!!!</s><br /><br /><i>come find me:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/ReadsAsh">www.facebook.com/ReadsAsh</a><br /><b>IG:</b> ash.reads <b>Twitter:</b> @ReadsAsh</i></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog">Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  </a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373211104" href="/book/show/18006096-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631826839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2490855167873193005"> Wow this book was really good! I loved everything about it, the plot was addicting and full of surprises!I loved the world Jennifer created. Jennifer creates a world filled with gargoyles who are called the "Wardens" and they are against the demons who have escaped Hell. It's unique the storyline, I haven't read something like this before!<br/><br/>Layla isn't so ordinary... because she is half gargoyle and half demon.. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394536187i/8867779.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Layla has been living so many years with the Warden's. Her unique abilities help them</span>
  <span id="freeText2490855167873193005" style="display:none"> Wow this book was really good! I loved everything about it, the plot was addicting and full of surprises!I loved the world Jennifer created. Jennifer creates a world filled with gargoyles who are called the "Wardens" and they are against the demons who have escaped Hell. It's unique the storyline, I haven't read something like this before!<br><br>Layla isn't so ordinary... because she is half gargoyle and half demon.. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394536187i/8867779.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Layla has been living so many years with the Warden's. Her unique abilities help them track demons..She feel safe with them and especially with one of them Zayne, who was on her side from when she was child. Everything is going well for Layla..until one day she's attacked by a demon, and then everything changes..when another demon saved her... Roth who is an upper demon..and not only this he is gorgeous and cocky!!!<br>Layla tries to avoid Roth but appears to spend more time together . Layla starts to realise that maybe not everything she knows is true. Things are getting more dangerous as more Demons keep appearing trying to find Layla.<br>Can she trust Roth? Can she believe everything the Wardens tell her? Can she still trust Zayne?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393201166i/8675683.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Layla was an amazing heroine! She is sweet, strong and brave.The only reason I give this book 4 stars, is because sometimes she was a little childish and this bothered me..<br><br>Mmmmm Zayne or Roth?????<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380776841ra/3122196.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Both guys care a lot about Layla..But who will she choose???<br><br>While Zayne is sweet, Roth is dangerous hot and sexy. From the beginning, Layla has feelings for Zayne. But the thing is he is so protective and he is afraid to pursue a relationship with her, so he's almost like a brother figure for her . On the other hand Roth *sigh* is so different!He wants her from the beginning and doesn't deny it! He is protective and he will do anything for her!!The attraction between them is explosive!!<br><br>I'm so taken by this world! Once again, Jennifer manages to create a total convincing paranormal world! An amazing book with kickass characters!! This is a must read for everyone who loves paranormal! It will blow you away and leave you needing for more!!<br><br><b>Thank you &lt;33 Harlequin and Edelweiss for the ARC</b></span>

<div id="review_1347711873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347711873" />
    <a title="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34403359"><img alt="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469758679p2/34403359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347711873?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" href="/user/show/34403359">☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17455585-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34403359?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34403359?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347711873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11400649245844954943">This is my first Armentrout book and I know that it won't be my last. I definitely liked it and was pleasantly surprised. I had been reading many reviews on it and wasn't sure if I would want another love triangle.<br/><br/><b> Plot Summary </b><br/><br/>Layla I-don't-know-her-last-name has just turned seventeen. She's like your average teenage girl. She tags demons, works with a group of demon hunters, so of course has to like a demon. So, no, she's not normal but she really wants to be. She is half-gargoyle/Warden and h</span>
  <span id="freeText11400649245844954943" style="display:none">This is my first Armentrout book and I know that it won't be my last. I definitely liked it and was pleasantly surprised. I had been reading many reviews on it and wasn't sure if I would want another love triangle.<br><br><b> Plot Summary </b><br><br>Layla I-don't-know-her-last-name has just turned seventeen. She's like your average teenage girl. She tags demons, works with a group of demon hunters, so of course has to like a demon. So, no, she's not normal but she really wants to be. She is half-gargoyle/Warden and half-demon. This means that she has more abilities, including killer kisses, then the Wardens and also is why she can't mate or marry any of them. This is really bad for her since she has to stay apart from Zayne, her best friend and the Warden that she has liked since she was young. He is very kind and gorgeous and this the problem that much harder to endure.<br><br>Of course there is going to be another guy. His name is Roth. He is also gorgeous but unlike Zayne, he is a demon. And has tattoos and piercings, which totally work on him. He can be egotistical but he is kind to Layla. Layla is inexplicably drawn to the man who claims to know everything about her and everything that is going on or will happen. She doesn't need to hide her true self, her demon side, from Roth which also means that they can kiss without fear of losing his soul. Which is a good thing for both of them since they kiss <s> a couple of times </s> a lot.<br><br>Together they work together to figure out the cause of the recent demon activity and uprising that could possibly lead to the end of the world. In the process, Layla is torn between choosing between Roth and Zayne who is with the only family that she ever really had.<br><br><b> What I liked </b><br><br>The characters were pretty good for the most part.<br>I liked Layla and the fact that she was trying to do her best and help everyone. I thought that she could have been seen saving herself more though. Roth was hysterical and I was smiling or laughing at everything he said. From the little I learned about Zayne, I liked him but not as much as Roth. Stacey I didn't like so much because had been with every guy it seemed which is a lot different from Layla. Sam was pretty cool with his smartness.<br><br>The love triangle wasn't that pronounced. In the recent series that I've been reading, <i> The Tiger Saga </i>, there is the love triangle throughout the whole thing and it can sometimes get annoying. This never happened with this book. Instead the fact that Layla likes to guys is only brought up and talked about. Well, except for the end which brings up my next point.<br><br>The ending was a massive cliffhanger and was a little upsetting.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431011359ra/14786678.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400509ra/776259.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*mouth gaping and eyes blinking*<br>It took me a few seconds and a few times going back to realize what had happened. I still didn't like the result but it makes the book that much more enjoyable and the desire for the next one greater!<br><br><br><b> What I didn't like or could have been better </b><br><br>I already mentioned some of the characters but I'll go over it again. Layla was sometimes shown as weak and would have to be saved or saved instead of her fighting. She would try it to fight it but it usually didn't work out. Layla also repeatedly said that she wasn't pretty or not good enough. I know that sometimes teenagers think like that but it seemed to be accented too much. These two things are also similar to <i> The Tiger Saga </i>. Stacey was also a problem for me. The way that she also talked about sex or made sexual innuendos was annoying and I thought kind of unnecessary. She would make comments about some jock at the school checking out Layla and then her saying that Layla was still a virgin and making fun about it.<br><br>Roth and Zayne seemed almost too perfect. I know that they both had problems because of what they were but the whole time Layla seemed to be admiring their "hard stomachs" or "holding their rock hard forearms." I think that it would have been much more realistic if they had more physical flaws. Even Roth's tattoos and piercings made Layla seem to like him more.<br><br>It was kind of bizarre that the fact that there are demons wouldn't be known to people. I mean, they knew about Wardens and why else would they be there?<br><br><b> Overall </b><br><br>The book was written well. The plot was good even though to me it seemed to occasionally get confusing. There was a lot of jumping between fighting/learning action and romantic action. The characters were developed well or seemingly too fake or set up. There was a lot of action which was good and it definitely showed both sides of Layla and what they represented.<br><br>I can't wait to read the next one.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385043110ra/7055901.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11400649245844954943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_715688775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715688775" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715688775?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781488720789" href="/book/show/20562076-white-hot-kiss">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=gargoyles">gargoyles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715688775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5057080306123872167">White Hot Kiss is book one in The Dark Elements series by Jennifer L. Armentrout. First I want to say that I have not read very many gargoyle books so I didn’t know what to expect going into this. But lets be realistic here. This book was written by Jennifer Armentrout. So I knew it was going to be epic. And I was NOT disappointed.<br/><br/>In this world we have wardens that are gargoyles that look like humans except while they sleep or when they choose to shed their human skin as in during a fight. The w</span>
  <span id="freeText5057080306123872167" style="display:none">White Hot Kiss is book one in The Dark Elements series by Jennifer L. Armentrout. First I want to say that I have not read very many gargoyle books so I didn’t know what to expect going into this. But lets be realistic here. This book was written by Jennifer Armentrout. So I knew it was going to be epic. And I was NOT disappointed.<br><br>In this world we have wardens that are gargoyles that look like humans except while they sleep or when they choose to shed their human skin as in during a fight. The world knows about them, they have gone public. Then there are the demons. This is the reason for the wardens. But, the world does not know about the demons. They walk among us every day disguised as humans so we don’t see them, but the wardens do. The wardens patrol the earth every night to rid the world of the demons, to protect the humans.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/demon_zpsa2cea0af.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1393787701i/8763384.jpg" alt=" photo demon_zpsa2cea0af.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then we have our main character, Layla. She is seventeen years old and is half warden and half demon. She was adopted into a family of wardens about 10 years ago, raised as a warden. But cannot shift like a warden can. Demons have the ability to suck the soul out of a human or a warden and Layla has this ability. So as a result, she can never kiss a boy, she can never kiss the handsome Zayne who she was raised with. Who she has had a crush on since the day she was brought into the house. Zayne is 21 years old. His father, Abbott wants him to choose a female, have children, but Zayne says he’s not ready. It obvious he feels more for Layla than he wants to. But even though its never spoken, its obvious he knows it can never be. <br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/gargoyle_zps3e09de52.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390360004i/8197542.jpg" alt=" photo gargoyle_zps3e09de52.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Then, there is Roth. There has to be a sexy bad boy right?! Roth is a demon. He keeps turning up when Layla needs saving. And that seems to be happening more and more often. And the more we get to know him, the more we fall for him, as does Layla. And demons don’t have souls, so the whole kissing problem, well, its not a problem with Roth.<br><br>What I didn’t expect, though, with this book, is to feel so emotionally involved. Layla is not accepted by most of the Warden world. She is half demon and Wardens hate demons. So where does she belong? I felt so bad for her struggling with this. And as she and Roth spend time together it was obvious that feelings were developing. So why is Roth protecting her? Why do these demons keep trying to kill her? Can she really trust Roth? <br><br>I was hooked from the first page to the last page and was left with my heart pounding. Layla has so much ahead of her and I can’t wait to find out what it is. I will leave you with my favorite line of the entire book. Who says it to whom? You will have to read it to find out.<br><br> <b>
  <i>“I lost myself the moment I found you.”</i>
</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5057080306123872167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
